BT 26.250 518.952 Td /F1 9.8 Tf \[(on how veterinarian staff and laboratory personnel can clinically manage esoteric, unexplained, or post-mortum examinations.  )\] TJ ET

BT 26.250 495.143 Td /F1 9.8 Tf \[(management of F. tularensis, and clinical findings on a case of feline tularemia are discussed. It further raises questions as to )\] TJ ET
BT 26.250 483.238 Td /F1 9.8 Tf \[(whether or not dead animals should be treated as sentinels and be pre-screened for select agents, especially in instances of )\] TJ ET
BT 26.250 471.333 Td /F1 9.8 Tf \[(dual diagnoses.)\] TJ ET
BT 26.250 451.929 Td /F1 9.8 Tf \[(Methods: A necropsy was performed on the cat by the Fort Riley veterinarian, DNA extraction and PCR analyses were )\] TJ ET

BT 26.250 361.095 Td /F1 9.8 Tf \[(using a Joint Biological Agent Identification and Diagnostic System \\(JBAIDS\\) Tularemia Detection Kit to detect a presumptive )\] TJ ET
BT 26.250 349.191 Td /F1 9.8 Tf \[(qualitative result to detect tularemia in feline and blood samples.   USAMRIID also performed RT-PCR and identified genomic )\] TJ ET
BT 26.250 337.286 Td /F1 9.8 Tf \[(DNA from F. tularensis Type A, \\(SPL15.013.02\\), thus confirming the FADL’s initial presumptive result of F. tularensis.  )\] TJ ET
BT 26.250 325.381 Td /F1 9.8 Tf \[(USAMRIID attempted to culture F. tularensis from three samples \\(swab, feline tissue, and transfer pipette tip\\), but no growth )\] TJ ET
